     <h1 class="api-title">WebView</h1> 
     <p> <code class="api-signature"> public class WebView </code> <br> <code class="api-signature"> </code> <code class="api-signature"> </code> <code class="api-signature"> </code> <code class="api-signature"> extends <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/AbsoluteLayout.html">AbsoluteLayout</a> </code> <code class="api-signature"> implements <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewTreeObserver.OnGlobalFocusChangeListener.html">ViewTreeObserver.OnGlobalFocusChangeListener</a>, <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.OnHierarchyChangeListener.html">ViewGroup.OnHierarchyChangeListener</a> </code> </p>
     <table class="jd-inheritance-table"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td colspan="5" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell"><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Object.html">java.lang.Object</a> </td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?</td> 
        <td colspan="4" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell"><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html">android.view.View</a> </td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?</td> 
        <td colspan="3" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell"><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html">android.view.ViewGroup</a> </td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;?</td> 
        <td colspan="2" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell"><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/AbsoluteLayout.html">android.widget.AbsoluteLayout</a> </td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td> 
        <td class="jd-inheritance-space">&nbsp;</td>

        <td colspan="1" class="jd-inheritance-class-cell">android.webkit.WebView </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <br>
     <hr> 
     <p></p>
     <p>A View that displays web pages. This class is the basis upon which you can roll your own web browser or simply display some online content within your Activity. It uses the WebKit rendering engine to display web pages and includes methods to navigate forward and backward through a history, zoom in and out, perform text searches and more.</p> 
     <p>Note that, in order for your Activity to access the Internet and load web pages in a WebView, you must add the <code>INTERNET</code> permissions to your Android Manifest file:</p> 
     <pre>&lt;uses-permission android:name="android.permission.INTERNET" /&gt;</pre> 
     <p>This must be a child of the <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/manifest-element.html"><code>&lt;manifest&gt;</code></a> element.</p> 
     <p>For more information, read <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/webapps/webview.html">Building Web Apps in WebView</a>.</p> 
     <h3>Basic usage</h3> 
     <p>By default, a WebView provides no browser-like widgets, does not enable JavaScript and web page errors are ignored. If your goal is only to display some HTML as a part of your UI, this is probably fine; the user won't need to interact with the web page beyond reading it, and the web page won't need to interact with the user. If you actually want a full-blown web browser, then you probably want to invoke the Browser application with a URL Intent rather than show it with a WebView. For example: </p>
     <pre>
 Uri uri = Uri.parse("https://www.example.com");
 Intent intent = new Intent(Intent.ACTION_VIEW, uri);
 startActivity(intent);
 </pre> 
     <p>See <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/Intent.html">Intent</a></code> for more information.</p> 
     <p>To provide a WebView in your own Activity, include a <code>&lt;WebView&gt;</code> in your layout, or set the entire Activity window as a WebView during <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Activity.html#onCreate(android.os.Bundle)">onCreate()</a></code>:</p> 
     <pre class="prettyprint">
 WebView webview = new WebView(this);
 setContentView(webview);
 </pre> 
     <p>Then load the desired web page:</p> 
     <pre>
 // Simplest usage: note that an exception will NOT be thrown
 // if there is an error loading this page (see below).
 webview.loadUrl("https://example.com/");

 // OR, you can also load from an HTML string:
 String summary = "&lt;html&gt;&lt;body&gt;You scored &lt;b&gt;192&lt;/b&gt; points.&lt;/body&gt;&lt;/html&gt;";
 webview.loadData(summary, "text/html", null);
 // ... although note that there are restrictions on what this HTML can do.
 // See the JavaDocs for <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadData(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">loadData()</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadDataWithBaseURL(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">loadDataWithBaseURL()</a></code> for more info.
 </pre> 
     <p>A WebView has several customization points where you can add your own behavior. These are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Creating and setting a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html">WebChromeClient</a></code> subclass. This class is called when something that might impact a browser UI happens, for instance, progress updates and JavaScript alerts are sent here (see <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/developing/debug-tasks.html#DebuggingWebPages">Debugging Tasks</a>). </li> 
      <li>Creating and setting a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebViewClient.html">WebViewClient</a></code> subclass. It will be called when things happen that impact the rendering of the content, eg, errors or form submissions. You can also intercept URL loading here (via <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebViewClient.html#shouldOverrideUrlLoading(android.webkit.WebView, java.lang.String)">shouldOverrideUrlLoading()</a></code>).</li> 
      <li>Modifying the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html">WebSettings</a></code>, such as enabling JavaScript with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#setJavaScriptEnabled(boolean)">setJavaScriptEnabled()</a></code>. </li> 
      <li>Injecting Java objects into the WebView using the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#addJavascriptInterface(java.lang.Object, java.lang.String)">addJavascriptInterface(Object, String)</a></code> method. This method allows you to inject Java objects into a page's JavaScript context, so that they can be accessed by JavaScript in the page.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Here's a more complicated example, showing error handling, settings, and progress notification:</p> 
     <pre class="prettyprint">
 // Let's display the progress in the activity title bar, like the
 // browser app does.
 getWindow().requestFeature(Window.FEATURE_PROGRESS);

 webview.getSettings().setJavaScriptEnabled(true);

 final Activity activity = this;
 webview.setWebChromeClient(new WebChromeClient() {
   public void onProgressChanged(WebView view, int progress) {
     // Activities and WebViews measure progress with different scales.
     // The progress meter will automatically disappear when we reach 100%
     activity.setProgress(progress * 1000);
   }
 });
 webview.setWebViewClient(new WebViewClient() {
   public void onReceivedError(WebView view, int errorCode, String description, String failingUrl) {
     Toast.makeText(activity, "Oh no! " + description, Toast.LENGTH_SHORT).show();
   }
 });

 webview.loadUrl("https://developer.android.com/");
 </pre> 
     <h3>Zoom</h3> 
     <p>To enable the built-in zoom, set <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#getSettings()">WebSettings</a></code>.<code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#setBuiltInZoomControls(boolean)">setBuiltInZoomControls(boolean)</a></code> (introduced in API level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#CUPCAKE">CUPCAKE</a></code>).</p> 
     <p>NOTE: Using zoom if either the height or width is set to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#WRAP_CONTENT">WRAP_CONTENT</a></code> may lead to undefined behavior and should be avoided.</p> 
     <h3>Cookie and window management</h3> 
     <p>For obvious security reasons, your application has its own cache, cookie store etc.it does not share the Browser application's data. </p> 
     <p>By default, requests by the HTML to open new windows are ignored. This is true whether they be opened by JavaScript or by the target attribute on a link. You can customize your <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html">WebChromeClient</a></code> to provide your own behavior for opening multiple windows, and render them in whatever manner you want.</p> 
     <p>The standard behavior for an Activity is to be destroyed and recreated when the device orientation or any other configuration changes. This will cause the WebView to reload the current page. If you don't want that, you can set your Activity to handle the <code>orientation</code> and <code>keyboardHidden</code> changes, and then just leave the WebView alone. It'll automatically re-orient itself as appropriate. Read <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/resources/runtime-changes.html">Handling Runtime Changes</a> for more information about how to handle configuration changes during runtime.</p> 
     <h3>Building web pages to support different screen densities</h3> 
     <p>The screen density of a device is based on the screen resolution. A screen with low density has fewer available pixels per inch, where a screen with high density has more  sometimes significantly more  pixels per inch. The density of a screen is important because, other things being equal, a UI element (such as a button) whose height and width are defined in terms of screen pixels will appear larger on the lower density screen and smaller on the higher density screen. For simplicity, Android collapses all actual screen densities into three generalized densities: high, medium, and low.</p> 
     <p>By default, WebView scales a web page so that it is drawn at a size that matches the default appearance on a medium density screen. So, it applies 1.5x scaling on a high density screen (because its pixels are smaller) and 0.75x scaling on a low density screen (because its pixels are bigger). Starting with API level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#ECLAIR">ECLAIR</a></code>, WebView supports DOM, CSS, and meta tag features to help you (as a web developer) target screens with different screen densities.</p> 
     <p>Here's a summary of the features you can use to handle different screen densities:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <code>window.devicePixelRatio</code> DOM property. The value of this property specifies the default scaling factor used for the current device. For example, if the value of <code>window.devicePixelRatio</code> is "1.0", then the device is considered a medium density (mdpi) device and default scaling is not applied to the web page; if the value is "1.5", then the device is considered a high density device (hdpi) and the page content is scaled 1.5x; if the value is "0.75", then the device is considered a low density device (ldpi) and the content is scaled 0.75x.</li> 
      <li>The <code>-webkit-device-pixel-ratio</code> CSS media query. Use this to specify the screen densities for which this style sheet is to be used. The corresponding value should be either "0.75", "1", or "1.5", to indicate that the styles are for devices with low density, medium density, or high density screens, respectively. For example: <pre>
 &lt;link rel="stylesheet" media="screen and (-webkit-device-pixel-ratio:1.5)" href="hdpi.css" /&gt;</pre> <p>The <code>hdpi.css</code> stylesheet is only used for devices with a screen pixel ration of 1.5, which is the high density pixel ratio.</p> </li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3>HTML5 Video support</h3> 
     <p>In order to support inline HTML5 video in your application you need to have hardware acceleration turned on. </p> 
     <h3>Full screen support</h3> 
     <p>In order to support full screen  for video or other HTML content  you need to set a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html">WebChromeClient</a></code> and implement both <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html#onShowCustomView(android.view.View, android.webkit.WebChromeClient.CustomViewCallback)">onShowCustomView(View, WebChromeClient.CustomViewCallback)</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html#onHideCustomView()">onHideCustomView()</a></code>. If the implementation of either of these two methods is missing then the web contents will not be allowed to enter full screen. Optionally you can implement <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html#getVideoLoadingProgressView()">getVideoLoadingProgressView()</a></code> to customize the View displayed whilst a video is loading. </p> 
     <h3>HTML5 Geolocation API support</h3> 
     <p>For applications targeting Android N and later releases (API level &gt; <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#M">M</a></code>) the geolocation api is only supported on secure origins such as https. For such applications requests to geolocation api on non-secure origins are automatically denied without invoking the corresponding <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebChromeClient.html#onGeolocationPermissionsShowPrompt(java.lang.String, android.webkit.GeolocationPermissions.Callback)">onGeolocationPermissionsShowPrompt(String, GeolocationPermissions.Callback)</a></code> method. </p> 
     <h3>Layout size</h3> 
     <p> It is recommended to set the WebView layout height to a fixed value or to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#MATCH_PARENT">MATCH_PARENT</a></code> instead of using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#WRAP_CONTENT">WRAP_CONTENT</a></code>. When using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#MATCH_PARENT">MATCH_PARENT</a></code> for the height none of the WebView's parents should use a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#WRAP_CONTENT">WRAP_CONTENT</a></code> layout height since that could result in incorrect sizing of the views. </p> 
     <p>Setting the WebView's height to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#WRAP_CONTENT">WRAP_CONTENT</a></code> enables the following behaviors: </p>
     <ul> 
      <li>The HTML body layout height is set to a fixed value. This means that elements with a height relative to the HTML body may not be sized correctly. </li> 
      <li>For applications targeting <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#KITKAT">KITKAT</a></code> and earlier SDKs the HTML viewport meta tag will be ignored in order to preserve backwards compatibility. </li> 
     </ul> 
     <p></p> 
     <p> Using a layout width of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.LayoutParams.html#WRAP_CONTENT">WRAP_CONTENT</a></code> is not supported. If such a width is used the WebView will attempt to use the width of the parent instead. </p> 
     <h3>Metrics</h3> 
     <p> WebView may upload anonymous diagnostic data to Google when the user has consented. This data helps Google improve WebView. Data is collected on a per-app basis for each app which has instantiated a WebView. An individual app can opt out of this feature by putting the following tag in its manifest: </p>
     <pre>
 &lt;meta-data android:name="android.webkit.WebView.MetricsOptOut"
            android:value="true" /&gt;
 </pre> 
     <p></p> 
     <p> Data will only be uploaded for a given app if the user has consented AND the app has not opted out. </p> 
     <p></p>

int RENDERER_PRIORITY_BOUND</pre>

      <div class="api-level">
        added in 
       <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int RENDERER_PRIORITY_IMPORTANT</pre>

Use with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#setRendererPriorityPolicy(int, boolean)">setRendererPriorityPolicy(int, boolean)</a></code>. </p>

     <a name="RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED</h3> 
      <div class="api-level">
        added in 
       <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED</pre> 
      <p>The renderer associated with this WebView is bound with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/Context.html#BIND_WAIVE_PRIORITY">BIND_WAIVE_PRIORITY</a></code>. At this priority level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> renderers will be strong targets for out of memory killing. Use with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#setRendererPriorityPolicy(int, boolean)">setRendererPriorityPolicy(int, boolean)</a></code>. </p>
      <p></p> 
      <p>Constant Value: 0 (0x00000000) </p>

       </div>

                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/util/AttributeSet.html">AttributeSet</a> attrs, 
                int defStyleAttr, 
                boolean privateBrowsing)</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This constructor was deprecated in API level 17.</strong><br> Private browsing is no longer supported directly via WebView and will be removed in a future release. Prefer using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html">WebSettings</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebViewDatabase.html">WebViewDatabase</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/CookieManager.html">CookieManager</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebStorage.html">WebStorage</a></code> for fine-grained control of privacy data. </p> 
      <p>Constructs a new WebView with layout parameters and a default style.</p>

void addJavascriptInterface (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/Object.html">Object</a> object, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> name)</pre> 
      <p>Injects the supplied Java object into this WebView. The object is injected into the JavaScript context of the main frame, using the supplied name. This allows the Java object's methods to be accessed from JavaScript. For applications targeted to API level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN_MR1">JELLY_BEAN_MR1</a></code> and above, only public methods that are annotated with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/JavascriptInterface.html">JavascriptInterface</a></code> can be accessed from JavaScript. For applications targeted to API level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN">JELLY_BEAN</a></code> or below, all public methods (including the inherited ones) can be accessed, see the important security note below for implications. </p>
      <p> Note that injected objects will not appear in JavaScript until the page is next (re)loaded. For example: </p>
      <pre>
 class JsObject {
    @JavascriptInterface
    public String toString() { return "injectedObject"; }
 }
 webView.addJavascriptInterface(new JsObject(), "injectedObject");
 webView.loadData("<title></title>", "text/html", null);
 webView.loadUrl("javascript:alert(injectedObject.toString())");</pre> 
      <p> <strong>IMPORTANT:</strong> </p>
      <ul> 
       <li> This method can be used to allow JavaScript to control the host application. This is a powerful feature, but also presents a security risk for apps targeting <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN">JELLY_BEAN</a></code> or earlier. Apps that target a version later than <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN">JELLY_BEAN</a></code> are still vulnerable if the app runs on a device running Android earlier than 4.2. The most secure way to use this method is to target <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN_MR1">JELLY_BEAN_MR1</a></code> and to ensure the method is called only when running on Android 4.2 or later. With these older versions, JavaScript could use reflection to access an injected object's public fields. Use of this method in a WebView containing untrusted content could allow an attacker to manipulate the host application in unintended ways, executing Java code with the permissions of the host application. Use extreme care when using this method in a WebView which could contain untrusted content.</li> 
       <li> JavaScript interacts with Java object on a private, background thread of this WebView. Care is therefore required to maintain thread safety. </li> 
       <li> The Java object's fields are not accessible.</li> 
       <li> For applications targeted to API level <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#LOLLIPOP">LOLLIPOP</a></code> and above, methods of injected Java objects are enumerable from JavaScript.</li> 
      </ul>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>object</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Object</code>: the Java object to inject into this WebView's JavaScript context. Null values are ignored.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>name</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the name used to expose the object in JavaScript <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="autofill(android.util.SparseArray<android.view.autofill.AutofillValue>)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">autofill</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void autofill (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/util/SparseArray.html">SparseArray</a>&lt;<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillValue.html">AutofillValue</a>&gt; values)</pre> 
      <p>Automatically fills the content of the virtual children within this view. </p>
      <p>Views with virtual children support the Autofill Framework mainly by: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>Providing the metadata defining what the virtual children mean and how they can be autofilled. </li>
       <li>Implementing the methods that autofill the virtual children. </li>
      </ul> 
      <p><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure(android.view.ViewStructure, int)">onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure(ViewStructure, int)</a></code> is responsible for the former, this method is responsible for the latter - see <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#autofill(android.view.autofill.AutofillValue)">autofill(AutofillValue)</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure(android.view.ViewStructure, int)">onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure(ViewStructure, int)</a></code> for more info about autofill. </p>
      <p>If a child value is updated asynchronously, the next call to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#notifyValueChanged(android.view.View, int, android.view.autofill.AutofillValue)">notifyValueChanged(View, int, AutofillValue)</a></code> must happen <b>after</b> the value was changed to the autofilled value. If not, the child will not be considered autofilled. </p>
      <p><b>Note:</b> To indicate that a virtual view was autofilled, <code>?android:attr/autofilledHighlight</code> should be drawn over it until the data changes.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>values</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>SparseArray</code>: map of values to be autofilled, keyed by virtual child id.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="capturePicture()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">capturePicture</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Picture.html">Picture</a> capturePicture ()</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This method was deprecated in API level 19.</strong><br> Use <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)">onDraw(Canvas)</a></code> to obtain a bitmap snapshot of the WebView, or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#saveWebArchive(java.lang.String)">saveWebArchive(String)</a></code> to save the content to a file. </p> 
      <p>Gets a new picture that captures the current contents of this WebView. The picture is of the entire document being displayed, and is not limited to the area currently displayed by this WebView. Also, the picture is a static copy and is unaffected by later changes to the content being displayed. </p>
      <p> Note that due to internal changes, for API levels between <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#HONEYCOMB">HONEYCOMB</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#ICE_CREAM_SANDWICH">ICE_CREAM_SANDWICH</a></code> inclusive, the picture does not include fixed position elements or scrollable divs. </p>
      <p> Note that from <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#JELLY_BEAN_MR1">JELLY_BEAN_MR1</a></code> the returned picture should only be drawn into bitmap-backed Canvas - using any other type of Canvas will involve additional conversion at a cost in memory and performance. Also the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Picture.html#createFromStream(java.io.InputStream)">createFromStream(InputStream)</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Picture.html#writeToStream(java.io.OutputStream)">writeToStream(OutputStream)</a></code> methods are not supported on the returned object.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Picture.html">Picture</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">a picture that captures the current contents of this WebView <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="createPrintDocumentAdapter(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-21"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">createPrintDocumentAdapter</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 21</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/print/PrintDocumentAdapter.html">PrintDocumentAdapter</a> createPrintDocumentAdapter (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> documentName)</pre> 
      <p>Creates a PrintDocumentAdapter that provides the content of this WebView for printing. The adapter works by converting the WebView contents to a PDF stream. The WebView cannot be drawn during the conversion process - any such draws are undefined. It is recommended to use a dedicated off screen WebView for the printing. If necessary, an application may temporarily hide a visible WebView by using a custom PrintDocumentAdapter instance wrapped around the object returned and observing the onStart and onFinish methods. See <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/print/PrintDocumentAdapter.html">PrintDocumentAdapter</a></code> for more information.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>documentName</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: The user-facing name of the printed document. See <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/print/PrintDocumentInfo.html">PrintDocumentInfo</a></code> <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr>

     <a name="enableSlowWholeDocumentDraw()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-21"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">enableSlowWholeDocumentDraw</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 21</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void enableSlowWholeDocumentDraw ()</pre> 
      <p>For apps targeting the L release, WebView has a new default behavior that reduces memory footprint and increases performance by intelligently choosing the portion of the HTML document that needs to be drawn. These optimizations are transparent to the developers. However, under certain circumstances, an App developer may want to disable them: </p>
      <ol> 
       <li>When an app uses <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)">onDraw(Canvas)</a></code> to do own drawing and accesses portions of the page that is way outside the visible portion of the page.</li> 
       <li>When an app uses <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#capturePicture()">capturePicture()</a></code> to capture a very large HTML document. Note that capturePicture is a deprecated API.</li> 
      </ol> Enabling drawing the entire HTML document has a significant performance cost. This method should be called before any WebViews are created. 
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
     </div> 
     <a name="evaluateJavascript(java.lang.String, android.webkit.ValueCallback<java.lang.String>)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-19"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">evaluateJavascript</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 19</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void evaluateJavascript (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> script, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/ValueCallback.html">ValueCallback</a>&lt;<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a>&gt; resultCallback)</pre> 
      <p>Asynchronously evaluates JavaScript in the context of the currently displayed page. If non-null, |resultCallback| will be invoked with any result returned from that execution. This method must be called on the UI thread and the callback will be made on the UI thread. </p>
      <p> Compatibility note. Applications targeting <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Build.VERSION_CODES.html#N">N</a></code> or later, JavaScript state from an empty WebView is no longer persisted across navigations like <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadUrl(java.lang.String)">loadUrl(String)</a></code>. For example, global variables and functions defined before calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadUrl(java.lang.String)">loadUrl(String)</a></code> will not exist in the loaded page. Applications should use <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#addJavascriptInterface(java.lang.Object, java.lang.String)">addJavascriptInterface(Object, String)</a></code> instead to persist JavaScript objects across navigations.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>script</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the JavaScript to execute.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>resultCallback</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>ValueCallback</code>: A callback to be invoked when the script execution completes with the result of the execution (if any). May be null if no notification of the result is required. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="findAddress(java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">findAddress</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> findAddress (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> addr)</pre> 
      <p>Gets the first substring consisting of the address of a physical location. Currently, only addresses in the United States are detected, and consist of: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>a house number</li> 
       <li>a street name</li> 
       <li>a street type (Road, Circle, etc), either spelled out or abbreviated</li> 
       <li>a city name</li> 
       <li>a state or territory, either spelled out or two-letter abbr</li> 
       <li>an optional 5 digit or 9 digit zip code</li> 
      </ul> All names must be correctly capitalized, and the zip code, if present, must be valid for the state. The street type must be a standard USPS spelling or abbreviation. The state or territory must also be spelled or abbreviated using USPS standards. The house number may not exceed five digits.
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>addr</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the string to search for addresses<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the address, or if no address is found, null <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="getAccessibilityNodeProvider()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-16"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">getAccessibilityNodeProvider</h3> 
      <div class="api-level">

      <p>Gets the provider for managing a virtual view hierarchy rooted at this View and reported to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/accessibilityservice/AccessibilityService.html">AccessibilityService</a></code>s that explore the window content. </p>
      <p> If this method returns an instance, this instance is responsible for managing <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/accessibility/AccessibilityNodeInfo.html">AccessibilityNodeInfo</a></code>s describing the virtual sub-tree rooted at this View including the one representing the View itself. Similarly the returned instance is responsible for performing accessibility actions on any virtual view or the root view itself. </p> 
      <p> If an <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.AccessibilityDelegate.html">View.AccessibilityDelegate</a></code> has been specified via calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#setAccessibilityDelegate(android.view.View.AccessibilityDelegate)">setAccessibilityDelegate(AccessibilityDelegate)</a></code> its <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.AccessibilityDelegate.html#getAccessibilityNodeProvider(android.view.View)">getAccessibilityNodeProvider(View)</a></code> is responsible for handling this call. </p>

     <a name="getCurrentWebViewPackage()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">getCurrentWebViewPackage</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/pm/PackageInfo.html">PackageInfo</a> getCurrentWebViewPackage ()</pre> 
      <p>If WebView has already been loaded into the current process this method will return the package that was used to load it. Otherwise, the package that would be used if the WebView was loaded right now will be returned; this does not cause WebView to be loaded, so this information may become outdated at any time. The WebView package changes either when the current WebView package is updated, disabled, or uninstalled. It can also be changed through a Developer Setting. If the WebView package changes, any app process that has loaded WebView will be killed. The next time the app starts and loads WebView it will use the new WebView package instead.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive">

     <a name="getHitTestResult()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">getHitTestResult</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.HitTestResult.html">WebView.HitTestResult</a> getHitTestResult ()</pre> 
      <p>Gets a HitTestResult based on the current cursor node. If a HTML::a tag is found and the anchor has a non-JavaScript URL, the HitTestResult type is set to SRC_ANCHOR_TYPE and the URL is set in the "extra" field. If the anchor does not have a URL or if it is a JavaScript URL, the type will be UNKNOWN_TYPE and the URL has to be retrieved through <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#requestFocusNodeHref(android.os.Message)">requestFocusNodeHref(Message)</a></code> asynchronously. If a HTML::img tag is found, the HitTestResult type is set to IMAGE_TYPE and the URL is set in the "extra" field. A type of SRC_IMAGE_ANCHOR_TYPE indicates an anchor with a URL that has an image as a child node. If a phone number is found, the HitTestResult type is set to PHONE_TYPE and the phone number is set in the "extra" field of HitTestResult. If a map address is found, the HitTestResult type is set to GEO_TYPE and the address is set in the "extra" field of HitTestResult. If an email address is found, the HitTestResult type is set to EMAIL_TYPE and the email is set in the "extra" field of HitTestResult. Otherwise, HitTestResult type is set to UNKNOWN_TYPE. </p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.HitTestResult.html">WebView.HitTestResult</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">
          <!-- no returns description in source --><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="loadData(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">loadData</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void loadData (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> data, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> mimeType, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> encoding)</pre> 
      <p>Loads the given data into this WebView using a 'data' scheme URL. </p>
      <p> Note that JavaScript's same origin policy means that script running in a page loaded using this method will be unable to access content loaded using any scheme other than 'data', including 'http(s)'. To avoid this restriction, use <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadDataWithBaseURL(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">loadDataWithBaseURL()</a></code> with an appropriate base URL. </p>
      <p> The encoding parameter specifies whether the data is base64 or URL encoded. If the data is base64 encoded, the value of the encoding parameter must be 'base64'. For all other values of the parameter, including null, it is assumed that the data uses ASCII encoding for octets inside the range of safe URL characters and use the standard %xx hex encoding of URLs for octets outside that range. For example, '#', '%', '\', '?' should be replaced by %23, %25, %27, %3f respectively. </p>
      <p> The 'data' scheme URL formed by this method uses the default US-ASCII charset. If you need need to set a different charset, you should form a 'data' scheme URL which explicitly specifies a charset parameter in the mediatype portion of the URL and call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadUrl(java.lang.String)">loadUrl(String)</a></code> instead. Note that the charset obtained from the mediatype portion of a data URL always overrides that specified in the HTML or XML document itself.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>data</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: a String of data in the given encoding<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>mimeType</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the MIME type of the data, e.g. 'text/html'<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>encoding</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the encoding of the data <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="loadDataWithBaseURL(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">loadDataWithBaseURL</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void loadDataWithBaseURL (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> baseUrl, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> data, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> mimeType, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> encoding, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> historyUrl)</pre> 
      <p>Loads the given data into this WebView, using baseUrl as the base URL for the content. The base URL is used both to resolve relative URLs and when applying JavaScript's same origin policy. The historyUrl is used for the history entry. </p>
      <p> Note that content specified in this way can access local device files (via 'file' scheme URLs) only if baseUrl specifies a scheme other than 'http', 'https', 'ftp', 'ftps', 'about' or 'javascript'. </p>
      <p> If the base URL uses the data scheme, this method is equivalent to calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#loadData(java.lang.String, java.lang.String, java.lang.String)">loadData()</a></code> and the historyUrl is ignored, and the data will be treated as part of a data: URL. If the base URL uses any other scheme, then the data will be loaded into the WebView as a plain string (i.e. not part of a data URL) and any URL-encoded entities in the string will not be decoded. </p>
      <p> Note that the baseUrl is sent in the 'Referer' HTTP header when requesting subresources (images, etc.) of the page loaded using this method.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>baseUrl</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the URL to use as the page's base URL. If null defaults to 'about:blank'.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>data</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: a String of data in the given encoding<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>mimeType</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the MIMEType of the data, e.g. 'text/html'. If null, defaults to 'text/html'.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>encoding</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the encoding of the data<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>historyUrl</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>String</code>: the URL to use as the history entry. If null defaults to 'about:blank'. If non-null, this must be a valid URL. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="onGenericMotionEvent(android.view.MotionEvent)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-12"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onGenericMotionEvent</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 12</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean onGenericMotionEvent (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html">MotionEvent</a> event)</pre> 
      <p>Implement this method to handle generic motion events. </p>
      <p> Generic motion events describe joystick movements, mouse hovers, track pad touches, scroll wheel movements and other input events. The <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#getSource()">source</a></code> of the motion event specifies the class of input that was received. Implementations of this method must examine the bits in the source before processing the event. The following code example shows how this is done. </p>
      <p> Generic motion events with source class <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/InputDevice.html#SOURCE_CLASS_POINTER">SOURCE_CLASS_POINTER</a></code> are delivered to the view under the pointer. All other generic motion events are delivered to the focused view. </p> 
      <pre> public boolean onGenericMotionEvent(MotionEvent event) {
     if (event.isFromSource(InputDevice.SOURCE_CLASS_JOYSTICK)) {
         if (event.getAction() == MotionEvent.ACTION_MOVE) {
             // process the joystick movement...
             return true;
         }
     }
     if (event.isFromSource(InputDevice.SOURCE_CLASS_POINTER)) {
         switch (event.getAction()) {
             case MotionEvent.ACTION_HOVER_MOVE:
                 // process the mouse hover movement...
                 return true;
             case MotionEvent.ACTION_SCROLL:
                 // process the scroll wheel movement...
                 return true;
         }
     }
     return super.onGenericMotionEvent(event);
 }</pre>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>event</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>MotionEvent</code>: The generic motion event being processed.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">True if the event was handled, false otherwise. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onGlobalFocusChanged(android.view.View, android.view.View)"></a>

     <a name="onHoverEvent(android.view.MotionEvent)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-14"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onHoverEvent</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 14</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean onHoverEvent (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html">MotionEvent</a> event)</pre> 
      <p>Implement this method to handle hover events. </p>
      <p> This method is called whenever a pointer is hovering into, over, or out of the bounds of a view and the view is not currently being touched. Hover events are represented as pointer events with action <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_ENTER">ACTION_HOVER_ENTER</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_MOVE">ACTION_HOVER_MOVE</a></code>, or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_EXIT">ACTION_HOVER_EXIT</a></code>. </p> 
      <ul> 
       <li>The view receives a hover event with action <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_ENTER">ACTION_HOVER_ENTER</a></code> when the pointer enters the bounds of the view.</li> 
       <li>The view receives a hover event with action <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_MOVE">ACTION_HOVER_MOVE</a></code> when the pointer has already entered the bounds of the view and has moved.</li> 
       <li>The view receives a hover event with action <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#ACTION_HOVER_EXIT">ACTION_HOVER_EXIT</a></code> when the pointer has exited the bounds of the view or when the pointer is about to go down due to a button click, tap, or similar user action that causes the view to be touched.</li> 
      </ul> 
      <p> The view should implement this method to return true to indicate that it is handling the hover event, such as by changing its drawable state. </p>
      <p> The default implementation calls <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#setHovered(boolean)">setHovered(boolean)</a></code> to update the hovered state of the view when a hover enter or hover exit event is received, if the view is enabled and is clickable. The default implementation also sends hover accessibility events. </p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>event</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>MotionEvent</code>: The motion event that describes the hover.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">True if the view handled the hover event.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onKeyDown(int, android.view.KeyEvent)"></a>

        <tr> 
         <td><code>keyCode</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: A key code that represents the button pressed, from <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.html">KeyEvent</a></code>.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>repeatCount</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The number of times the action was made.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>event</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>KeyEvent</code>: The KeyEvent object that defines the button action. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">If you handled the event, return true. If you want to allow the event to be handled by the next receiver, return false. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onKeyUp(int, android.view.KeyEvent)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onKeyUp</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean onKeyUp (int keyCode, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.html">KeyEvent</a> event)</pre> 
      <p>Default implementation of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.Callback.html#onKeyUp(int, android.view.KeyEvent)">KeyEvent.Callback.onKeyUp()</a></code>: perform clicking of the view when <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.html#KEYCODE_DPAD_CENTER">KEYCODE_DPAD_CENTER</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.html#KEYCODE_ENTER">KEYCODE_ENTER</a></code> or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/KeyEvent.html#KEYCODE_SPACE">KEYCODE_SPACE</a></code> is released. </p>
      <p>Key presses in software keyboards will generally NOT trigger this listener, although some may elect to do so in some situations. Do not rely on this to catch software key presses.</p>

        </tr> 
        <tr>

     <a name="onPause()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-11"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onPause</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 11</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onPause ()</pre> 
      <p>Does a best-effort attempt to pause any processing that can be paused safely, such as animations and geolocation. Note that this call does not pause JavaScript. To pause JavaScript globally, use <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#pauseTimers()">pauseTimers()</a></code>. To resume WebView, call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#onResume()">onResume()</a></code>. </p>
      <p></p> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure(android.view.ViewStructure, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onProvideAutofillVirtualStructure (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html">ViewStructure</a> structure, 
                int flags)</pre> 
      <p>Populates a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html">ViewStructure</a></code> containing virtual children to fullfil an autofill request. </p>
      <p>This method should be used when the view manages a virtual structure under this view. For example, a view that draws input fields using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#draw(android.graphics.Canvas)">draw(Canvas)</a></code>. </p>
      <p>When implementing this method, subclasses must follow the rules below: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>Add virtual children by calling the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#newChild(int)">newChild(int)</a></code> or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#asyncNewChild(int)">asyncNewChild(int)</a></code> methods, where the <code>id</code> is an unique id identifying the children in the virtual structure. </li>
       <li>The children hierarchy can have multiple levels if necessary, but ideally it should exclude intermediate levels that are irrelevant for autofill; that would improve the autofill performance. </li>
       <li>Also implement <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#autofill(android.util.SparseArray<android.view.autofill.AutofillValue>)">autofill(SparseArray)</a></code> to autofill the virtual children. </li>
       <li>Set the autofill properties of the child structure as defined by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onProvideAutofillStructure(android.view.ViewStructure, int)">onProvideAutofillStructure(ViewStructure, int)</a></code>, using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setAutofillId(android.view.autofill.AutofillId, int)">setAutofillId(AutofillId, int)</a></code> to set its autofill id. </li>
       <li>Call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#notifyViewEntered(android.view.View, int, android.graphics.Rect)">notifyViewEntered(View, int, Rect)</a></code> and/or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#notifyViewExited(android.view.View, int)">notifyViewExited(View, int)</a></code> when the focused virtual child changed. </li>
       <li>Call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#notifyValueChanged(android.view.View, int, android.view.autofill.AutofillValue)">notifyValueChanged(View, int, AutofillValue)</a></code> when the value of a virtual child changed. </li>
       <li>Call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#commit()">commit()</a></code> when the autofill context of the view structure changed and the current context should be committed (for example, when the user tapped a <code>SUBMIT</code> button in an HTML page). </li>
       <li>Call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#cancel()">cancel()</a></code> when the autofill context of the view structure changed and the current context should be canceled (for example, when the user tapped a <code>CANCEL</code> button in an HTML page). </li>
       <li>Provide ways for users to manually request autofill by calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#requestAutofill(android.view.View, int, android.graphics.Rect)">requestAutofill(View, int, Rect)</a></code>. </li>
       <li>The <code>left</code> and <code>top</code> values set in <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setDimens(int, int, int, int, int, int)">setDimens(int, int, int, int, int, int)</a></code> must be relative to the next <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#isImportantForAutofill()">isImportantForAutofill()</a></code> predecessor view included in the structure. </li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Views with virtual children support the Autofill Framework mainly by: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>Providing the metadata defining what the virtual children mean and how they can be autofilled. </li>
       <li>Implementing the methods that autofill the virtual children. </li>
      </ul> 
      <p>This method is responsible for the former; <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#autofill(android.util.SparseArray<android.view.autofill.AutofillValue>)">autofill(SparseArray)</a></code> is responsible for the latter. </p>
      <p>The <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html">ViewStructure</a></code> traditionally represents a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html">View</a></code>, while for web pages it represent HTML nodes. Hence, it's necessary to "map" the HTML properties in a way that is understood by the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/service/autofill/AutofillService.html">AutofillService</a></code> implementations: </p>
      <ol> 
       <li>Only the HTML nodes inside a <code>FORM</code> are generated. </li>
       <li>The source of the HTML is set using <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setWebDomain(java.lang.String)">setWebDomain(String)</a></code> in the node representing the WebView. </li>
       <li>If a web page has multiple <code>FORM</code>s, only the data for the current form is representedif the user taps a field from another form, then the current autofill context is canceled (by calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/autofill/AutofillManager.html#cancel()">cancel()</a></code> and a new context is created for that <code>FORM</code>. </li>
       <li>Similarly, if the page has <code>IFRAME</code> nodes, they are not initially represented in the view structure until the user taps a field from a <code>FORM</code> inside the <code>IFRAME</code>, in which case it would be treated the same way as multiple forms described above, except that the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setWebDomain(java.lang.String)">web domain</a></code> of the <code>FORM</code> contains the <code>src</code> attribute from the <code>IFRAME</code> node. </li>
       <li>If the Android SDK provides a similar View, then should be set with the fully-qualified class name of such view. </li>
       <li>The W3C autofill field (<code>autocomplete</code> tag attribute) maps to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setAutofillHints(java.lang.String[])">setAutofillHints(String[])</a></code>. </li>
       <li>The <code>type</code> attribute of <code>INPUT</code> tags maps to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setInputType(int)">setInputType(int)</a></code>. </li>
       <li>The <code>value</code> attribute of <code>INPUT</code> tags maps to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setText(java.lang.CharSequence)">setText(CharSequence)</a></code>. </li>
       <li>If the view is editalbe, the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setAutofillType(int)">setAutofillType(int)</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setAutofillValue(android.view.autofill.AutofillValue)">setAutofillValue(AutofillValue)</a></code> must be set. </li>
       <li>The <code>placeholder</code> attribute maps to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setHint(java.lang.CharSequence)">setHint(CharSequence)</a></code>. </li>
       <li>Other HTML attributes can be represented through <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewStructure.html#setHtmlInfo(android.view.ViewStructure.HtmlInfo)">setHtmlInfo(android.view.ViewStructure.HtmlInfo)</a></code>. </li>
      </ol> 
      <p>It should also call <code>structure.setDataIsSensitive(false)</code> for fields whose value were not dynamically changed (for example, through Javascript). </p>
      <p>Example1: an HTML form with 2 fields for username and password. </p>
      <pre class="prettyprint">
    &lt;input type="text" name="username" id="user" value="Type your username" autocomplete="username" placeholder="Email or username"&gt;
    &lt;input type="password" name="password" id="pass" autocomplete="current-password" placeholder="Password"&gt;
 </pre> 
      <p>Would map to: </p>
      <pre class="prettyprint">
     int index = structure.addChildCount(2);
     ViewStructure username = structure.newChild(index);
     username.setAutofillId(structure.getAutofillId(), 1); // id 1 - first child
     username.setClassName("input");
     username.setInputType("android.widget.EditText");
     username.setAutofillHints("username");
     username.setHtmlInfo(username.newHtmlInfoBuilder("input")
         .addAttribute("type", "text")
         .addAttribute("name", "username")
         .addAttribute("id", "user")
         .build());
     username.setHint("Email or username");
     username.setAutofillType(View.AUTOFILL_TYPE_TEXT);
     username.setAutofillValue(AutofillValue.forText("Type your username"));
     username.setText("Type your username");
     // Value of the field is not sensitive because it was not dynamically changed:
     username.setDataIsSensitive(false);

     ViewStructure password = structure.newChild(index + 1);
     username.setAutofillId(structure, 2); // id 2 - second child
     password.setInputType("android.widget.EditText");
     password.setInputType(InputType.TYPE_TEXT_VARIATION_PASSWORD);
     password.setAutofillHints("current-password");
     password.setHtmlInfo(password.newHtmlInfoBuilder("input")
         .addAttribute("type", "password")
         .addAttribute("name", "password")
         .addAttribute("id", "pass")
         .build());
     password.setHint("Password");
     password.setAutofillType(View.AUTOFILL_TYPE_TEXT);
 </pre> 
      <p>Example2: an IFRAME tag. </p>
      <pre class="prettyprint">
    &lt;iframe src="https://example.com/login"/&gt;
 </pre> 
      <p>Would map to: </p>
      <pre class="prettyprint">
     int index = structure.addChildCount(1);
     ViewStructure iframe = structure.newChildFor(index);
     iframe.setAutofillId(structure.getAutofillId(), 1);
     iframe.setHtmlInfo(iframe.newHtmlInfoBuilder("iframe")
         .addAttribute("src", "https://example.com/login")
         .build());
 </pre> 
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>structure</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>ViewStructure</code>: fill in with virtual children data for autofill purposes.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>flags</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: optional flags.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

The defaullt implementation uses <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#getAccessibilityNodeProvider()">getAccessibilityNodeProvider()</a></code> to try to generate this from the view's virtual accessibility nodes, if any.      <a name="onTouchEvent(android.view.MotionEvent)"></a>

      <p>Implement this method to handle touch screen motion events. </p>
      <p> If this method is used to detect click actions, it is recommended that the actions be performed by implementing and calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#performClick()">performClick()</a></code>. This will ensure consistent system behavior, including: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>obeying click sound preferences </li>
       <li>dispatching OnClickListener calls </li>
       <li>handling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/accessibility/AccessibilityNodeInfo.html#ACTION_CLICK">ACTION_CLICK</a></code> when accessibility features are enabled </li>

boolean onTrackballEvent (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html">MotionEvent</a> event)</pre> 
      <p>Implement this method to handle trackball motion events. The <em>relative</em> movement of the trackball since the last event can be retrieve with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#getX()">MotionEvent.getX()</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/MotionEvent.html#getY()">MotionEvent.getY()</a></code>. These are normalized so that a movement of 1 corresponds to the user pressing one DPAD key (so they will often be fractional values, representing the more fine-grained movement information available from a trackball).</p>

      <p>Called when the window containing this view gains or loses focus. Note that this is separate from view focus: to receive key events, both your view and its window must have focus.      <a name="postVisualStateCallback(long, android.webkit.WebView.VisualStateCallback)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-23"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">postVisualStateCallback</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 23</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void postVisualStateCallback (long requestId, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html">WebView.VisualStateCallback</a> callback)</pre> 
      <p>Posts a <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html">WebView.VisualStateCallback</a></code>, which will be called when the current state of the WebView is ready to be drawn. </p>
      <p>Because updates to the DOM are processed asynchronously, updates to the DOM may not immediately be reflected visually by subsequent <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)">onDraw(Canvas)</a></code> invocations. The <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html">WebView.VisualStateCallback</a></code> provides a mechanism to notify the caller when the contents of the DOM at the current time are ready to be drawn the next time the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> draws.</p> 
      <p>The next draw after the callback completes is guaranteed to reflect all the updates to the DOM up to the point at which the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html">WebView.VisualStateCallback</a></code> was posted, but it may also contain updates applied after the callback was posted.</p> 
      <p>The state of the DOM covered by this API includes the following: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>primitive HTML elements (div, img, span, etc..)</li> 
       <li>images</li> 
       <li>CSS animations</li> 
       <li>WebGL</li> 
       <li>canvas</li> 
      </ul> It does not include the state of: 
      <ul> 
       <li>the video tag</li> 
      </ul>
      <p></p> 
      <p>To guarantee that the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> will successfully render the first frame after the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html#onComplete(long)">onComplete(long)</a></code> method has been called a set of conditions must be met: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>If the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code>'s visibility is set to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#VISIBLE">VISIBLE</a></code> then the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> must be attached to the view hierarchy.</li> 
       <li>If the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code>'s visibility is set to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#INVISIBLE">INVISIBLE</a></code> then the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> must be attached to the view hierarchy and must be made <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#VISIBLE">VISIBLE</a></code> from the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html#onComplete(long)">onComplete(long)</a></code> method.</li> 
       <li>If the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code>'s visibility is set to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#GONE">GONE</a></code> then the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> must be attached to the view hierarchy and its <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/AbsoluteLayout.LayoutParams.html">LayoutParams</a></code>'s width and height need to be set to fixed values and must be made <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#VISIBLE">VISIBLE</a></code> from the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.VisualStateCallback.html#onComplete(long)">onComplete(long)</a></code> method.</li> 
      </ul>
      <p></p> 
      <p>When using this API it is also recommended to enable pre-rasterization if the <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code> is off screen to avoid flickering. See <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#setOffscreenPreRaster(boolean)">setOffscreenPreRaster(boolean)</a></code> for more details and do consider its caveats.</p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>requestId</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>long</code>: An id that will be returned in the callback to allow callers to match requests with callbacks.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>callback</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>WebView.VisualStateCallback</code>: The callback to be invoked. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="postWebMessage(android.webkit.WebMessage, android.net.Uri)"></a>

     <a name="requestChildRectangleOnScreen(android.view.View, android.graphics.Rect, boolean)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">requestChildRectangleOnScreen</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean requestChildRectangleOnScreen (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html">View</a> child, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Rect.html">Rect</a> rect, 
                boolean immediate)</pre> 
      <p>Called when a child of this group wants a particular rectangle to be positioned onto the screen. <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html">ViewGroup</a></code>s overriding this can trust that: </p>
      <ul> 
       <li>child will be a direct child of this group</li> 
       <li>rectangle will be in the child's content coordinates</li> 
      </ul> 
      <p><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html">ViewGroup</a></code>s overriding this should uphold the contract:</p> 
      <ul> 
       <li>nothing will change if the rectangle is already visible</li> 
       <li>the view port will be scrolled only just enough to make the rectangle visible</li> 
       <ul>
        <p></p>
        <p></p> 
        <table class="responsive"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
          </tr>
