           <td width="100%"> <code>View</code>: The direct child making the request.<p></p></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><code>rect</code></td> 
           <td width="100%"> <code>Rect</code>: The rectangle in the child's coordinates the child wishes to be on the screen.<p></p></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><code>immediate</code></td> 
           <td width="100%"> <code>boolean</code>: True to forbid animated or delayed scrolling, false otherwise<p></p></td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <table class="responsive"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr>
           <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
          </tr>

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </ul>
      </ul>

     <a name="requestFocus(int, android.graphics.Rect)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">requestFocus</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean requestFocus (int direction, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Rect.html">Rect</a> previouslyFocusedRect)</pre> 
      <p>Call this to try to give focus to a specific view or to one of its descendants and give it hints about the direction and a specific rectangle that the focus is coming from. The rectangle can help give larger views a finer grained hint about where focus is coming from, and therefore, where to show selection, or forward focus change internally. A view will not actually take focus if it is not focusable (<code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#isFocusable()">isFocusable()</a></code> returns false), or if it is focusable and it is not focusable in touch mode (<code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#isFocusableInTouchMode()">isFocusableInTouchMode()</a></code>) while the device is in touch mode. A View will not take focus if it is not visible. A View will not take focus if one of its parents has <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html#getDescendantFocusability()">getDescendantFocusability()</a></code> equal to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html#FOCUS_BLOCK_DESCENDANTS">FOCUS_BLOCK_DESCENDANTS</a></code>. See also <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#focusSearch(int)">focusSearch(int)</a></code>, which is what you call to say that you have focus, and you want your parent to look for the next one. You may wish to override this method if your custom <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html">View</a></code> has an internal <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html">View</a></code> that it wishes to forward the request to. Looks for a view to give focus to respecting the setting specified by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html#getDescendantFocusability()">getDescendantFocusability()</a></code>. Uses <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/ViewGroup.html#onRequestFocusInDescendants(int, android.graphics.Rect)">onRequestFocusInDescendants(int, android.graphics.Rect)</a></code> to find focus within the children of this group when appropriate.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>direction</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: One of FOCUS_UP, FOCUS_DOWN, FOCUS_LEFT, and FOCUS_RIGHT<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>previouslyFocusedRect</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Rect</code>: The rectangle (in this View's coordinate system) to give a finer grained hint about where focus is coming from. May be null if there is no hint.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>boolean</code></td> 
         <td width="100%">Whether this view or one of its descendants actually took focus. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="requestFocusNodeHref(android.os.Message)"></a>

      <p>Requests the anchor or image element URL at the last tapped point. If hrefMsg is null, this method returns immediately and does not dispatch hrefMsg to its target. If the tapped point hits an image, an anchor, or an image in an anchor, the message associates strings in named keys in its data. The value paired with the key may be an empty string.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>hrefMsg</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Message</code>: the message to be dispatched with the result of the request. The message data contains three keys. "url" returns the anchor's href attribute. "title" returns the anchor's text. "src" returns the image's src attribute. <p></p></td>

     <a name="restoreState(android.os.Bundle)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">restoreState</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">

      <p>Restores the state of this WebView from the given Bundle. This method is intended for use in <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Activity.html#onRestoreInstanceState(android.os.Bundle)">onRestoreInstanceState(Bundle)</a></code> and should be called to restore the state of this WebView. If it is called after this WebView has had a chance to build state (load pages, create a back/forward list, etc.) there may be undesirable side-effects. Please note that this method no longer restores the display data for this WebView.</p>

         <th colspan="2">Returns</th>
        </tr>

         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebBackForwardList.html">WebBackForwardList</a></code></td> 
         <td width="100%">the restored back/forward list or null if restoreState failed <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

     <a name="resumeTimers()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">resumeTimers</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void resumeTimers ()</pre> 
      <p>Resumes all layout, parsing, and JavaScript timers for all WebViews. This will resume dispatching all timers. </p>

                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/java/lang/String.html">String</a> password)</pre> 
      <p> </p>
      <p class="caution"><strong> This method was deprecated in API level 18.</strong><br> Saving passwords in WebView will not be supported in future versions. </p> 
      <p>Sets a username and password pair for the specified host. This data is used by the WebView to autocomplete username and password fields in web forms. Note that this is unrelated to the credentials used for HTTP authentication.</p>

     <a name="saveState(android.os.Bundle)"></a>

      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>

      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebBackForwardList.html">WebBackForwardList</a> saveState (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/os/Bundle.html">Bundle</a> outState)</pre> 
      <p>Saves the state of this WebView used in <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Activity.html#onSaveInstanceState(android.os.Bundle)">onSaveInstanceState(Bundle)</a></code>. Please note that this method no longer stores the display data for this WebView. The previous behavior could potentially leak files if <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#restoreState(android.os.Bundle)">restoreState(Bundle)</a></code> was never called.</p>

         <td><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebBackForwardList.html">WebBackForwardList</a></code></td>

     <a name="setInitialScale(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">setInitialScale</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void setInitialScale (int scaleInPercent)</pre> 
      <p>Sets the initial scale for this WebView. 0 means default. The behavior for the default scale depends on the state of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#getUseWideViewPort()">getUseWideViewPort()</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#getLoadWithOverviewMode()">getLoadWithOverviewMode()</a></code>. If the content fits into the WebView control by width, then the zoom is set to 100%. For wide content, the behavior depends on the state of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebSettings.html#getLoadWithOverviewMode()">getLoadWithOverviewMode()</a></code>. If its value is true, the content will be zoomed out to be fit by width into the WebView control, otherwise not. If initial scale is greater than 0, WebView starts with this value as initial scale. Please note that unlike the scale properties in the viewport meta tag, this method doesn't take the screen density into account.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>scaleInPercent</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the initial scale in percent <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="setLayerType(int, android.graphics.Paint)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-11"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">setLayerType</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 11</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void setLayerType (int layerType, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Paint.html">Paint</a> paint)</pre> 
      <p></p>
      <p>Specifies the type of layer backing this view. The layer can be <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_NONE">LAYER_TYPE_NONE</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE">LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE</a></code> or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE">LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE</a></code>.</p> 
      <p>A layer is associated with an optional <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Paint.html">Paint</a></code> instance that controls how the layer is composed on screen. The following properties of the paint are taken into account when composing the layer:</p> 
      <ul> 
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Paint.html#getAlpha()">Translucency (alpha)</a></code></li> 
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Paint.html#getXfermode()">Blending mode</a></code></li> 
       <li><code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Paint.html#getColorFilter()">Color filter</a></code></li> 
      </ul> 
      <p>If this view has an alpha value set to &lt; 1.0 by calling <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#setAlpha(float)">setAlpha(float)</a></code>, the alpha value of the layer's paint is superseded by this view's alpha value.</p> 
      <p>Refer to the documentation of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_NONE">LAYER_TYPE_NONE</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE">LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE">LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE</a></code> for more information on when and how to use layers.</p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>layerType</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The type of layer to use with this view, must be one of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_NONE">LAYER_TYPE_NONE</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE">LAYER_TYPE_SOFTWARE</a></code> or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE">LAYER_TYPE_HARDWARE</a></code><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>paint</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Paint</code>: The paint used to compose the layer. This argument is optional and can be null. It is ignored when the layer type is <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#LAYER_TYPE_NONE">LAYER_TYPE_NONE</a></code><p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="setOverScrollMode(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-9">

      <div class="api-level">

      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void setOverScrollMode (int mode)</pre> 
      <p>Set the over-scroll mode for this view. Valid over-scroll modes are <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#OVER_SCROLL_ALWAYS">OVER_SCROLL_ALWAYS</a></code> (default), <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#OVER_SCROLL_IF_CONTENT_SCROLLS">OVER_SCROLL_IF_CONTENT_SCROLLS</a></code> (allow over-scrolling only if the view content is larger than the container), or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#OVER_SCROLL_NEVER">OVER_SCROLL_NEVER</a></code>. Setting the over-scroll mode of a view will have an effect only if the view is capable of scrolling.</p>

     <a name="setPictureListener(android.webkit.WebView.PictureListener)"></a>

     <a name="setRendererPriorityPolicy(int, boolean)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-26"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">setRendererPriorityPolicy</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 26</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void setRendererPriorityPolicy (int rendererRequestedPriority, 
                boolean waivedWhenNotVisible)</pre> 
      <p>Set the renderer priority policy for this <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html">WebView</a></code>. The priority policy will be used to determine whether an out of process renderer should be considered to be a target for OOM killing. Because a renderer can be associated with more than one WebView, the final priority it is computed as the maximum of any attached WebViews. When a WebView is destroyed it will cease to be considerered when calculating the renderer priority. Once no WebViews remain associated with the renderer, the priority of the renderer will be reduced to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED">RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED</a></code>. The default policy is to set the priority to <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#RENDERER_PRIORITY_IMPORTANT">RENDERER_PRIORITY_IMPORTANT</a></code> regardless of visibility, and this should not be changed unless the caller also handles renderer crashes with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebViewClient.html#onRenderProcessGone(android.webkit.WebView, android.webkit.RenderProcessGoneDetail)">onRenderProcessGone(WebView, RenderProcessGoneDetail)</a></code>. Any other setting will result in WebView renderers being killed by the system more aggressively than the application.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>rendererRequestedPriority</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the minimum priority at which this WebView desires the renderer process to be bound.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>waivedWhenNotVisible</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>boolean</code>: if true, this flag specifies that when this WebView is not visible, it will be treated as if it had requested a priority of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/webkit/WebView.html#RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED">RENDERER_PRIORITY_WAIVED</a></code>. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="setScrollBarStyle(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">setScrollBarStyle</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void setScrollBarStyle (int style)</pre> 
      <p></p>
      <p>Specify the style of the scrollbars. The scrollbars can be overlaid or inset. When inset, they add to the padding of the view. And the scrollbars can be drawn inside the padding area or on the edge of the view. For example, if a view has a background drawable and you want to draw the scrollbars inside the padding specified by the drawable, you can use SCROLLBARS_INSIDE_OVERLAY or SCROLLBARS_INSIDE_INSET. If you want them to appear at the edge of the view, ignoring the padding, then you can use SCROLLBARS_OUTSIDE_OVERLAY or SCROLLBARS_OUTSIDE_INSET.</p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>style</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: the style of the scrollbars. Should be one of SCROLLBARS_INSIDE_OVERLAY, SCROLLBARS_INSIDE_INSET, SCROLLBARS_OUTSIDE_OVERLAY or SCROLLBARS_OUTSIDE_INSET.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div>

     <a name="shouldDelayChildPressedState()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-14"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">shouldDelayChildPressedState</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 14</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
boolean shouldDelayChildPressedState ()</pre> 
      <p>Return true if the pressed state should be delayed for children or descendants of this ViewGroup. Generally, this should be done for containers that can scroll, such as a List. This prevents the pressed state from appearing when the user is actually trying to scroll the content. The default implementation returns true for compatibility reasons. Subclasses that do not scroll should generally override this method and return false. </p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive">

     <a name="computeHorizontalScrollOffset()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">computeHorizontalScrollOffset</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
int computeHorizontalScrollOffset ()</pre> 
      <p></p>
      <p>Compute the horizontal offset of the horizontal scrollbar's thumb within the horizontal range. This value is used to compute the position of the thumb within the scrollbar's track.</p> 
      <p>The range is expressed in arbitrary units that must be the same as the units used by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#computeHorizontalScrollRange()">computeHorizontalScrollRange()</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#computeHorizontalScrollExtent()">computeHorizontalScrollExtent()</a></code>.</p> 
      <p>The default offset is the scroll offset of this view.</p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p>

     <a name="onAttachedToWindow()"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onAttachedToWindow</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onAttachedToWindow ()</pre> 
      <p>This is called when the view is attached to a window. At this point it has a Surface and will start drawing. Note that this function is guaranteed to be called before <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)">onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)</a></code>, however it may be called any time before the first onDraw -- including before or after <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onMeasure(int, int)">onMeasure(int, int)</a></code>.</p>
      <p></p> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onConfigurationChanged(android.content.res.Configuration)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-8"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onConfigurationChanged</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 8</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onConfigurationChanged (<a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/res/Configuration.html">Configuration</a> newConfig)</pre> 
      <p>Called when the current configuration of the resources being used by the application have changed. You can use this to decide when to reload resources that can changed based on orientation and other configuration characteristics. You only need to use this if you are not relying on the normal <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/Activity.html">Activity</a></code> mechanism of recreating the activity instance upon a configuration change.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>newConfig</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Configuration</code>: The new resource configuration. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onDraw(android.graphics.Canvas)"></a>

     <a name="onFocusChanged(boolean, int, android.graphics.Rect)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onFocusChanged</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onFocusChanged (boolean focused, 
                int direction, 
                <a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/Rect.html">Rect</a> previouslyFocusedRect)</pre> 
      <p>Called by the view system when the focus state of this view changes. When the focus change event is caused by directional navigation, direction and previouslyFocusedRect provide insight into where the focus is coming from. When overriding, be sure to call up through to the super class so that the standard focus handling will occur.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>focused</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>boolean</code>: True if the View has focus; false otherwise.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>direction</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The direction focus has moved when requestFocus() is called to give this view focus. Values are <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_UP">FOCUS_UP</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_DOWN">FOCUS_DOWN</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_LEFT">FOCUS_LEFT</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_RIGHT">FOCUS_RIGHT</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_FORWARD">FOCUS_FORWARD</a></code>, or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#FOCUS_BACKWARD">FOCUS_BACKWARD</a></code>. It may not always apply, in which case use the default.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>previouslyFocusedRect</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>Rect</code>: The rectangle, in this view's coordinate system, of the previously focused view. If applicable, this will be passed in as finer grained information about where the focus is coming from (in addition to direction). Will be <code>null</code> otherwise. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onMeasure(int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onMeasure</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onMeasure (int widthMeasureSpec, 
                int heightMeasureSpec)</pre> 
      <p></p>
      <p> Measure the view and its content to determine the measured width and the measured height. This method is invoked by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#measure(int, int)">measure(int, int)</a></code> and should be overridden by subclasses to provide accurate and efficient measurement of their contents. </p> 
      <p> <strong>CONTRACT:</strong> When overriding this method, you <em>must</em> call <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#setMeasuredDimension(int, int)">setMeasuredDimension(int, int)</a></code> to store the measured width and height of this view. Failure to do so will trigger an <code>IllegalStateException</code>, thrown by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#measure(int, int)">measure(int, int)</a></code>. Calling the superclass' <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onMeasure(int, int)">onMeasure(int, int)</a></code> is a valid use. </p> 
      <p> The base class implementation of measure defaults to the background size, unless a larger size is allowed by the MeasureSpec. Subclasses should override <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#onMeasure(int, int)">onMeasure(int, int)</a></code> to provide better measurements of their content. </p> 
      <p> If this method is overridden, it is the subclass's responsibility to make sure the measured height and width are at least the view's minimum height and width (<code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#getSuggestedMinimumHeight()">getSuggestedMinimumHeight()</a></code> and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#getSuggestedMinimumWidth()">getSuggestedMinimumWidth()</a></code>). </p>
      <p></p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>widthMeasureSpec</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: horizontal space requirements as imposed by the parent. The requirements are encoded with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.MeasureSpec.html">View.MeasureSpec</a></code>.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>heightMeasureSpec</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: vertical space requirements as imposed by the parent. The requirements are encoded with <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.MeasureSpec.html">View.MeasureSpec</a></code>.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <a name="onOverScrolled(int, int, boolean, boolean)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-9">

void onOverScrolled (int scrollX, 
                int scrollY,

      <p>Called by <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#overScrollBy(int, int, int, int, int, int, int, int, boolean)">overScrollBy(int, int, int, int, int, int, int, int, boolean)</a></code> to respond to the results of an over-scroll operation.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>scrollY</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: New Y scroll value in pixels<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr>

         <td width="100%"> <code>boolean</code>: True if scrollX was clamped to an over-scroll boundary<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr>

       </tbody>

     </div> 
     <a name="onScrollChanged(int, int, int, int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onScrollChanged</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in

      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onScrollChanged (int l, 
                int t, 
                int oldl, 
                int oldt)</pre> 
      <p>This is called in response to an internal scroll in this view (i.e., the view scrolled its own contents). This is typically as a result of <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#scrollBy(int, int)">scrollBy(int, int)</a></code> or <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#scrollTo(int, int)">scrollTo(int, int)</a></code> having been called.</p>

         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: Current vertical scroll origin.<p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>oldl</code></td>

        </tr> 
        <tr>

     <a name="onWindowVisibilityChanged(int)"></a> 
     <div class="api apilevel-1"> 
      <h3 class="api-name">onWindowVisibilityChanged</h3> 
      <div class="api-level"> 
       <div>
         added in 
        <a href="https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/manifest/uses-sdk-element.html#ApiLevels">API level 1</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <pre class="api-signature no-pretty-print">
void onWindowVisibilityChanged (int visibility)</pre> 
      <p>Called when the window containing has change its visibility (between <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#GONE">GONE</a></code>, <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#INVISIBLE">INVISIBLE</a></code>, and <code><a href="https://developer.android.com/reference/android/view/View.html#VISIBLE">VISIBLE</a></code>). Note that this tells you whether or not your window is being made visible to the window manager; this does <em>not</em> tell you whether or not your window is obscured by other windows on the screen, even if it is itself visible.</p>
      <p></p> 
      <table class="responsive"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2">Parameters</th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><code>visibility</code></td> 
         <td width="100%"> <code>int</code>: The new visibility of the window. <p></p></td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>
